كتاب البيع
ومنه شرط خيار مؤقت معلوم زائد على الثلاثة ومنه استثناء حمل الجارية، ومنه الرضا ففسد المكره وشراؤه وكذا البيع تلجئة ويملك الأول بالقبض دون الثاني. ومنها الفائدة بيع ما فبيع لا فائدة فيه وشراؤه فاسد، ففسد بيع درهم بدرهم استويا وزناً وصفة؛ كذا في الذخيرة. وأما الخاصة فمنها معلومية الأجل في البيع بثمن مؤجل ففسد إن كان مجهولاً، ومنها القبض في بيع المشتري المنقول وفي الدين فبيع الدين قبل قبضه فاسد كالمسلم فيه، ورأس المال ولو بعد الإقالة، وبيع شيء بالدين الذي على فلان بخلاف ما إذا كان على البائع. ومنها أن يكون البدل مسمى في أحد نوعي المبادلة وهي القولية، فإن سكت عنه فسد وملك بالقبض، وإن نفاه قيل فسد وقيل بطل فلا يملك بالقبض. وفي التتمة باعه بدين عليه وهما يعلمان أن عليه لم يصح ومنها المماثلة بين البدلين في أموال الربا وسيأتي تفصيله في بابه. ومنها الخلو عن شبهة الربا، ومنها وجود شرائط السلم الآتية، ومنها القبض في الصرف قبل الافتراق ومنها أن يكون الثمن الأول معلوماً في بيع المرابحة والتولية والإشراك والوضيعة. وأما شرائط اللزوم بعد الانعقاد والنفاذ فخلوه من الخيارات الأربعة المشهورة، ويزاد خيار الكمية وخيار الغبن إذا كان فيه غرور، وخيار استحقاق بعض المبيع القيمي مطلقاً والمثلي قبل القبض، وخيار الخيانة في المرابحة وخيار نقد الثمن ،وعدمه وخيار كشف الحال، وخيار فوات وصف مرغوب فيه، وخيار إجازة بيع الفضولي وخيار هلاك بعض المبيع فهي ثلاثة يصح لم ينعقد لأن ما لا يصح منه منعقد كالفاسد ومنه غيره كالباطل وفي قوله «منعقد نافذ» نظر فإن بيع المكره من الفاسد كما قدمه وهو منعقد موقوف وكان الظاهر أن يقول منعقد مملوك تأمل . قوله : (ومنه شرط الأجل في البيع المعين والثمن المعين (الخ قال الرملي أقول في جواهر الفتاوى : رجل له على آخر حنطة غير السلم فباعها منه بثمن معلوم إلى شهر لا يجوز لأن هذا بيع الكاليء بالكاليء وقد نهينا عنه وإن باعها ممن عليه ونقد المشتري الثمن في المجلس جاز فيكون ديناً بعين اهـ. وقد ذكر المسألة في منح الغفار في باب القرض قبل باب الربا نقلاً عن البزازية، وسيأتي في شرح قوله ويباع الطعام كيلاً وجزافاً» نقلاً عن البزازية : له عليه حنطة أكلها فباعها منه نسيئة لا يجوز. أقول : ومثله الزيت وكل مكيل وموزون ومثل البيع الصلح قال في الفصل الثلاثين من جامع الفصولين: ولو غصب كربر فصالحه وهو قائم على دراهم مؤجلة جاز، وكذا الذهب والفضة وسائر الموزونات، ولو صالحه على كيل مؤجل لم يجز إذ الجنس بانفراده يحرم النساء، ولو كان البر هالكاً لم يجز الصلح على شيء من هذا نسيئة لأنه دين بدين إلا إذا صالح على بر مثله أو أقل منه مؤجلاً جاز لأنه عين حقه والحط جائز لا لو على أكثر للربا والصلح على بعض حقه في الكيلي والوزني حال قيامه لم يجز اهـ. وذكر في البزارية الحيلة في جواز بيع الجنطة المستهلكة بالنسيئة أنه يبيعها بثوب ويقبض الثوب ثم يبيعه بدراهم إلى أجل أقول وتجري هذه الحيلة في الصلح أيضاً. وقد صارت جملة الشرائط ستة وسبعين فشرائط الانعقاد أحد عشر، وشرائط النفاذ اثنان، وشرائط الصحة خمسة وعشرون وشرط اللزوم واحد بعد اجتماع الكل، فعلى هذا شرائط اللزوم تسعة وثلاثون، والكل من غير تداخل ثمانية وسبب شرعيته تعلق البقاء المعلوم فيه الله تعالى على وجه جميل. وأما أحكامه فالأصلي له الملك في البدلين لكل منهما في بدل، وهو في اللغة القوة والقدرة، وشرعاً ما قدمناه والتابع وجوب تسليم المبيع والثمن ووجوب استبراء الجارية على المشتري وملك الاستمتاع بالجارية وثبوت الشفعة لو كان عقاراً وعتق المبيع لو كان محرماً من البائع. وأما صفة ذلك الحكم فاللزوم عند عدم خيار فليس لأحدهما فسخه فالبيع عند عدم الخيار من العقود اللازمة والعقود ثلاثة لازم من الطرفين وهو البيع والسلم والإجارة - وإن قلنا بفسخها بالأعذار - والصلح والحوالة والمساقاة والوصية بعد القبول بعد موت الموصي والنكاح والصداق والصدقة المقبوضة والهبة المقبوضة إذا وجد مانع من الموانع السبعة الآتية. ولازم من أحد الجانبين وهو الرهن فإنه لازم من جهة الراهن بعد التسليم دون المرتهن وجائز من الطرفين فلكل منهما فسخه وهو الشركة والوكالة والعارية لغير الراهن والمضاربة والوديعة والقضاء والوصاية قبل قبول الوصي، وأما بعده فلازمة والوصية قبل موت الموصي. وأما أنواعه فبالنظر إلى مطلق البيع أربعة : نافذ وموقوف وفاسد وباطل . فالنافذ ما أفاد الحكم للحال والموقوف ما أفاده عند الإجازة، والفاسد ما أفاده عند القبض، والباطل ما لم يفده أصلاً؛ كذا في الحاوي وغيره وهو ظاهر في أن الموقوف ليس من الفاسد وإنما هو إما من قسم الصحيح أو قسم برأسه وهو ظاهر كلامهم وبالنظر إلى المبيع أربعة : مقايضة وهي بيع العين بالعين وبيع الدين بالدين وهو الصرف وبيع الدين بالعين وهو السلم وعكسه وهو بيع العين بالدين كأكثر البياعات وبالنظر إلى الثمن خمسة: مرابحة وتولية وإشراك ووضيعة ومساومة. وستأتي البيوع المكروهة. وأما محاسنه فمنها التوصل إلى الأغراض وإخلاء العالم عن الفساد. وفي آخر بيوع البزازية قيل للإمام محمد : ألا تصنف في الزهد ؟ قال : حسبكم كتاب البيوع وكان التجار في القديم إذا سافروا استصحبوا معهم بد للتاجر من فقيه صديق اهـ. قال الشمني فقيهاً يرجعون إليه . أئمة . وعن خوارزم أنه لا وهي واقعة الفتوى ويكثر وقوع ذلك فاستفده .اهـ. قوله : (ستة وسبعين) فيه نظر لأن شرائط الانعقاد والنفاد والصحة ثمانية وثلاثون وشرائط اللزوم هذه المذكورات مع زيادة الخلو من الخيارات فصارت سبعة وسبعين، لكن علمت أن الصواب أن شرائط الانعقاد تسعة فيسقط منها اثنان، ومن شرائط الصحة اثنان أيضاً، ومن شرائط اللزوم أربعة فتبقى الجملة تسعة وستين. قوله : (والكل من غير تداخل ثمانية) لم يظهر لي مراده فتأمل. قوله : (لو كان محرماً من البائع) صوابه من المشتري .
Book of Sale. And from it is the condition of a temporary option known in addition to three, and from it is the exclusion of the slave-girl's pregnancy, and from it is consent, so the sale of the coerced person is corrupt and his purchase, and likewise the sale of talji'ah, and the first owns by possession but not the second. And from it is the benefit: selling what has no benefit and buying it is corrupt, so selling a dirham for a dirham equal in weight and quality is corrupt; as in al-Dhakhirah. As for the specific ones: from them is the knowledge of the term in a sale with a deferred price, so it is corrupt if unknown; and from them is possession in the buyer's sale of movables and in debt, so selling debt before taking possession is corrupt like the salam capital, even after annulment; and selling something for the debt owed by so-and-so, unlike if it is upon the seller. And from them is that the countervalue be specified in one of the two types of exchange, which is verbal; if silent about it, it is corrupt and ownership by possession; if denied, it is said corrupt and said void, so no ownership by possession. In al-Tatimmah: he sold it for a debt upon him while both know it is upon him, it is not valid. And from them is equality between the two countervalues in ribawi goods, and its detail will come in its chapter. And from them is freedom from suspicion of riba, and from them is the existence of the conditions of salam to come, and from them is possession in exchange before separation, and from them is that the first price be known in murabahah, tawliyah, ishrak, and wadi'ah sales. As for conditions of bindingness after conclusion and validity: freedom from the four well-known options, and added is option of quantity, option of deception if there is misrepresentation, option of entitlement of part of the sale item, option of treachery in murabahah, option of payment of price or its absence, option of investigation, option of loss of a desirable attribute, option of ratification of the unauthorized sale, option of destruction of part of the sale item—so there are three: valid not concluded because what is not valid from it is like corrupt, and other than it like void. And in his saying 'concluded valid' there is consideration, for the sale of the coerced is among the corrupt as he stated, and it is concluded but suspended...
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqā'iq, provides a comprehensive enumeration of the conditions (shurūṭ) of a valid sale (bay') according to the Hanafī school. The author begins by listing conditions that belong to the 'general' category, such as the requirement of an option (khiyār) for a known period not exceeding three days, the exclusion of the slave-girl's pregnancy from the sale (istithnā' ḥaml al-jāriyah), and the necessity of mutual consent (riḍā), explaining that a sale under coercion (mukrah) is fāsid (corrupt). He then distinguishes between conditions for validity (ṣiḥḥa) and bindingness (luzūm). For validity, he mentions knowledge of the term in a deferred sale, taking possession (qabḍ) before resale of movables, avoidance of debt-for-debt sale (bay' al-kālī' bi al-kālī'), specification of the countervalue, equality in ribawī goods, freedom from ribā suspicion, conditions of salam, and possession before separation in ṣarf. For bindingness, he lists freedom from the four famous options and additional options like khiyār al-ghubn (fraud) and khiyār al-'ayb (defect). The passage then discusses the classification of sales into nāfidh (effective), mawqūf (suspended), fāsid (corrupt), and bāṭil (void), explaining that a corrupt sale conveys ownership upon possession while a void one does not. It also categorizes sales by countervalue: muqāyaḍah (exchange), ṣarf (money exchange), salam, and ordinary sale. The author critiques the count of conditions (76 vs. 69) and ends with a narration about Imam Muhammad's emphasis on the book of sales. The commentary follows the structure: first general conditions, then specific ones for validity, then bindingness, then classifications, then a note on the count. Key Hanafī positions such as the sale of the coerced being fāsid and mawqūf (suspended) are highlighted.

Key Terms
فاسد (fāsid): A sale that is concluded (munʿaqid) but defective; it conveys ownership upon possession (bi al-qabḍ) but is not valid without that.
باطل (bāṭil): A sale that fails to meet any condition of conclusion; it does not transfer ownership at all.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what type of sale is a sale made under coercion (mukrah)?
A) Bāṭil (void)
B) Fāsid (corrupt)
C) Nāfidh (effective)
D) Mawqūf (suspended)

Key Takeaway
A coerced sale is fāsid, not bāṭil; ownership transfers only upon possession – a unique Hanafī position.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Specific Conditions for Validity (Shurūṭ al-Ṣiḥḥa)
Enumerating specific conditions for validity (ṣiḥḥa) of a sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the specific conditions required for the validity (ṣiḥḥa) of a sale in Hanafī fiqh and apply them to examples.

Core Idea
A valid sale requires knowledge of terms, correct possession, avoidance of ribā, and specific conditions for deferred and salam sales.

After the general conditions, the passage delves into the detailed prerequisites for a sale to be valid (ṣaḥīḥ). These include knowledge of the term in deferred sales, taking possession before reselling, avoiding debt sales, equality in ribawī goods, and more. Understanding these is crucial for any transaction to be Islamically sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition regarding the term in a deferred sale
The term (ajal) must be known; if unknown, the sale is fāsid.
Example: selling with a payment date of 'sometime next month' is invalid.
2
Recognize the possession condition for movables
A buyer cannot resell a movable item before taking physical possession; otherwise the sale is fāsid.
Applies to the buyer's sale of what he bought, not the original seller.
3
Understand the prohibition of debt sales
Selling a debt before taking possession is fāsid; also selling something for a debt owed by a third party (not the seller) is invalid.
Exception: selling for a debt that is upon the seller is allowed.
4
List the conditions related to ribā
1) Equality in ribawī goods (mumāthala). 2) Freedom from suspicion of ribā (khalā' ʿan shubhat al-ribā).
Details of ribawī goods will be given later.
5
Recall conditions for salam and ṣarf
Salam has its own conditions (mentioned later). For ṣarf (currency exchange), possession must occur before separation (qabḍ qabla al-iftirāq).

كتاب البيع
ومنه شرط خيار مؤقت معلوم زائد على الثلاثة ومنه استثناء حمل الجارية، ومنه الرضا ففسد المكره وشراؤه وكذا البيع تلجئة ويملك الأول بالقبض دون الثاني. ومنها الفائدة بيع ما فبيع لا فائدة فيه وشراؤه فاسد، ففسد بيع درهم بدرهم استويا وزناً وصفة؛ كذا في الذخيرة. وأما الخاصة فمنها معلومية الأجل في البيع بثمن مؤجل ففسد إن كان مجهولاً، ومنها القبض في بيع المشتري المنقول وفي الدين فبيع الدين قبل قبضه فاسد كالمسلم فيه، ورأس المال ولو بعد الإقالة، وبيع شيء بالدين الذي على فلان بخلاف ما إذا كان على البائع. ومنها أن يكون البدل مسمى في أحد نوعي المبادلة وهي القولية، فإن سكت عنه فسد وملك بالقبض، وإن نفاه قيل فسد وقيل بطل فلا يملك بالقبض. وفي التتمة باعه بدين عليه وهما يعلمان أن عليه لم يصح ومنها المماثلة بين البدلين في أموال الربا وسيأتي تفصيله في بابه. ومنها الخلو عن شبهة الربا، ومنها وجود شرائط السلم الآتية، ومنها القبض في الصرف قبل الافتراق ومنها أن يكون الثمن الأول معلوماً في بيع المرابحة والتولية والإشراك والوضيعة. وأما شرائط اللزوم بعد الانعقاد والنفاذ فخلوه من الخيارات الأربعة المشهورة، ويزاد خيار الكمية وخيار الغبن إذا كان فيه غرور، وخيار استحقاق بعض المبيع القيمي مطلقاً والمثلي قبل القبض، وخيار الخيانة في المرابحة وخيار نقد الثمن ،وعدمه وخيار كشف الحال، وخيار فوات وصف مرغوب فيه، وخيار إجازة بيع الفضولي وخيار هلاك بعض المبيع فهي ثلاثة يصح لم ينعقد لأن ما لا يصح منه منعقد كالفاسد ومنه غيره كالباطل وفي قوله «منعقد نافذ» نظر فإن بيع المكره من الفاسد كما قدمه وهو منعقد موقوف وكان الظاهر أن يقول منعقد مملوك تأمل . قوله : (ومنه شرط الأجل في البيع المعين والثمن المعين (الخ قال الرملي أقول في جواهر الفتاوى : رجل له على آخر حنطة غير السلم فباعها منه بثمن معلوم إلى شهر لا يجوز لأن هذا بيع الكاليء بالكاليء وقد نهينا عنه وإن باعها ممن عليه ونقد المشتري الثمن في المجلس جاز فيكون ديناً بعين اهـ. وقد ذكر المسألة في منح الغفار في باب القرض قبل باب الربا نقلاً عن البزازية، وسيأتي في شرح قوله ويباع الطعام كيلاً وجزافاً» نقلاً عن البزازية : له عليه حنطة أكلها فباعها منه نسيئة لا يجوز. أقول : ومثله الزيت وكل مكيل وموزون ومثل البيع الصلح قال في الفصل الثلاثين من جامع الفصولين: ولو غصب كربر فصالحه وهو قائم على دراهم مؤجلة جاز، وكذا الذهب والفضة وسائر الموزونات، ولو صالحه على كيل مؤجل لم يجز إذ الجنس بانفراده يحرم النساء، ولو كان البر هالكاً لم يجز الصلح على شيء من هذا نسيئة لأنه دين بدين إلا إذا صالح على بر مثله أو أقل منه مؤجلاً جاز لأنه عين حقه والحط جائز لا لو على أكثر للربا والصلح على بعض حقه في الكيلي والوزني حال قيامه لم يجز اهـ. وذكر في البزارية الحيلة في جواز بيع الجنطة المستهلكة بالنسيئة أنه يبيعها بثوب ويقبض الثوب ثم يبيعه بدراهم إلى أجل أقول وتجري هذه الحيلة في الصلح أيضاً. وقد صارت جملة الشرائط ستة وسبعين فشرائط الانعقاد أحد عشر، وشرائط النفاذ اثنان، وشرائط الصحة خمسة وعشرون وشرط اللزوم واحد بعد اجتماع الكل، فعلى هذا شرائط اللزوم تسعة وثلاثون، والكل من غير تداخل ثمانية وسبب شرعيته تعلق البقاء المعلوم فيه الله تعالى على وجه جميل. وأما أحكامه فالأصلي له الملك في البدلين لكل منهما في بدل، وهو في اللغة القوة والقدرة، وشرعاً ما قدمناه والتابع وجوب تسليم المبيع والثمن ووجوب استبراء الجارية على المشتري وملك الاستمتاع بالجارية وثبوت الشفعة لو كان عقاراً وعتق المبيع لو كان محرماً من البائع. وأما صفة ذلك الحكم فاللزوم عند عدم خيار فليس لأحدهما فسخه فالبيع عند عدم الخيار من العقود اللازمة والعقود ثلاثة لازم من الطرفين وهو البيع والسلم والإجارة - وإن قلنا بفسخها بالأعذار - والصلح والحوالة والمساقاة والوصية بعد القبول بعد موت الموصي والنكاح والصداق والصدقة المقبوضة والهبة المقبوضة إذا وجد مانع من الموانع السبعة الآتية. ولازم من أحد الجانبين وهو الرهن فإنه لازم من جهة الراهن بعد التسليم دون المرتهن وجائز من الطرفين فلكل منهما فسخه وهو الشركة والوكالة والعارية لغير الراهن والمضاربة والوديعة والقضاء والوصاية قبل قبول الوصي، وأما بعده فلازمة والوصية قبل موت الموصي. وأما أنواعه فبالنظر إلى مطلق البيع أربعة : نافذ وموقوف وفاسد وباطل . فالنافذ ما أفاد الحكم للحال والموقوف ما أفاده عند الإجازة، والفاسد ما أفاده عند القبض، والباطل ما لم يفده أصلاً؛ كذا في الحاوي وغيره وهو ظاهر في أن الموقوف ليس من الفاسد وإنما هو إما من قسم الصحيح أو قسم برأسه وهو ظاهر كلامهم وبالنظر إلى المبيع أربعة : مقايضة وهي بيع العين بالعين وبيع الدين بالدين وهو الصرف وبيع الدين بالعين وهو السلم وعكسه وهو بيع العين بالدين كأكثر البياعات وبالنظر إلى الثمن خمسة: مرابحة وتولية وإشراك ووضيعة ومساومة. وستأتي البيوع المكروهة. وأما محاسنه فمنها التوصل إلى الأغراض وإخلاء العالم عن الفساد. وفي آخر بيوع البزازية قيل للإمام محمد : ألا تصنف في الزهد ؟ قال : حسبكم كتاب البيوع وكان التجار في القديم إذا سافروا استصحبوا معهم بد للتاجر من فقيه صديق اهـ. قال الشمني فقيهاً يرجعون إليه . أئمة . وعن خوارزم أنه لا وهي واقعة الفتوى ويكثر وقوع ذلك فاستفده .اهـ. قوله : (ستة وسبعين) فيه نظر لأن شرائط الانعقاد والنفاد والصحة ثمانية وثلاثون وشرائط اللزوم هذه المذكورات مع زيادة الخلو من الخيارات فصارت سبعة وسبعين، لكن علمت أن الصواب أن شرائط الانعقاد تسعة فيسقط منها اثنان، ومن شرائط الصحة اثنان أيضاً، ومن شرائط اللزوم أربعة فتبقى الجملة تسعة وستين. قوله : (والكل من غير تداخل ثمانية) لم يظهر لي مراده فتأمل. قوله : (لو كان محرماً من البائع) صوابه من المشتري .
Book of Sale. And from it is the condition of a temporary option known in addition to three, and from it is the exclusion of the slave-girl's pregnancy, and from it is consent, so the sale of the coerced person is corrupt and his purchase, and likewise the sale of talji'ah, and the first owns by possession but not the second. And from it is the benefit: selling what has no benefit and buying it is corrupt, so selling a dirham for a dirham equal in weight and quality is corrupt; as in al-Dhakhirah. As for the specific ones: from them is the knowledge of the term in a sale with a deferred price, so it is corrupt if unknown; and from them is possession in the buyer's sale of movables and in debt, so selling debt before taking possession is corrupt like the salam capital, even after annulment; and selling something for the debt owed by so-and-so, unlike if it is upon the seller. And from them is that the countervalue be specified in one of the two types of exchange, which is verbal; if silent about it, it is corrupt and ownership by possession; if denied, it is said corrupt and said void, so no ownership by possession. In al-Tatimmah: he sold it for a debt upon him while both know it is upon him, it is not valid. And from them is equality between the two countervalues in ribawi goods, and its detail will come in its chapter. And from them is freedom from suspicion of riba, and from them is the existence of the conditions of salam to come, and from them is possession in exchange before separation, and from them is that the first price be known in murabahah, tawliyah, ishrak, and wadi'ah sales. As for conditions of bindingness after conclusion and validity: freedom from the four well-known options, and added is option of quantity, option of deception if there is misrepresentation, option of entitlement of part of the sale item, option of treachery in murabahah, option of payment of price or its absence, option of investigation, option of loss of a desirable attribute, option of ratification of the unauthorized sale, option of destruction of part of the sale item—so there are three: valid not concluded because what is not valid from it is like corrupt, and other than it like void. And in his saying 'concluded valid' there is consideration, for the sale of the coerced is among the corrupt as he stated, and it is concluded but suspended...
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqā'iq, provides a comprehensive enumeration of the conditions (shurūṭ) of a valid sale (bay') according to the Hanafī school. The author begins by listing conditions that belong to the 'general' category, such as the requirement of an option (khiyār) for a known period not exceeding three days, the exclusion of the slave-girl's pregnancy from the sale (istithnā' ḥaml al-jāriyah), and the necessity of mutual consent (riḍā), explaining that a sale under coercion (mukrah) is fāsid (corrupt). He then distinguishes between conditions for validity (ṣiḥḥa) and bindingness (luzūm). For validity, he mentions knowledge of the term in a deferred sale, taking possession (qabḍ) before resale of movables, avoidance of debt-for-debt sale (bay' al-kālī' bi al-kālī'), specification of the countervalue, equality in ribawī goods, freedom from ribā suspicion, conditions of salam, and possession before separation in ṣarf. For bindingness, he lists freedom from the four famous options and additional options like khiyār al-ghubn (fraud) and khiyār al-'ayb (defect). The passage then discusses the classification of sales into nāfidh (effective), mawqūf (suspended), fāsid (corrupt), and bāṭil (void), explaining that a corrupt sale conveys ownership upon possession while a void one does not. It also categorizes sales by countervalue: muqāyaḍah (exchange), ṣarf (money exchange), salam, and ordinary sale. The author critiques the count of conditions (76 vs. 69) and ends with a narration about Imam Muhammad's emphasis on the book of sales. The commentary follows the structure: first general conditions, then specific ones for validity, then bindingness, then classifications, then a note on the count. Key Hanafī positions such as the sale of the coerced being fāsid and mawqūf (suspended) are highlighted.

Key Terms
شرائط الصحة (shurūṭ al-ṣiḥḥa): Conditions for the validity of the contract (e.g., knowledge of price, avoidance of ribā).
ربا (ribā): Usury/interest; prohibited in Islamic law. Its suspicion must be avoided in sales.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a specific condition for validity according to the passage?
A) Knowledge of the term in deferred sale
B) Equality in ribawi goods
C) The sale must be in a mosque
D) Possession before separation in currency exchange

Key Takeaway
A valid sale must fulfill specific conditions; each omission renders the sale fāsid, requiring possession for ownership transfer.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Classification of Sales and Bindingness
Classifying sales by effect, countervalue, pricing, and listing conditions for bindingness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify sales into nāfidh, mawqūf, fāsid, and bāṭil, and state the conditions that make a sale binding (lāzim).

Core Idea
Sales are classified by their effect: nāfidh (effective), mawqūf (suspended), fāsid (corrupt), bāṭil (void); a sale becomes binding only when free from valid options.

The passage concludes with a comprehensive classification of sales from different perspectives: by their legal effect, by the type of countervalue, and by pricing method. It also outlines the conditions for a sale to become binding (luzūm), which include the absence of various options (khiyārāt). This framework is essential for understanding the rights of parties in a transaction.

Guided Path
1
Define the four categories by legal effect
Nāfidh: effective immediately. Mawqūf: effective upon ratification. Fāsid: effective upon possession. Bāṭil: never effective.
The text explicitly says: 'النافذ ما أفاد الحكم للحال والموقوف ما أفاده عند الإجازة، والفاسد ما أفاده عند القبض، والباطل ما لم يفده أصلاً'.
2
List the types by countervalue
Muqāyaḍah (exchange of goods), ṣarf (exchange of currency), salam (advance payment for future delivery), and ordinary sale (deferred payment).
These are based on what is sold and how.
3
List the types by pricing method
Murābaḥa (cost-plus), tawliya (at cost), ishrāk (partnership), wadī'a (discount), musāwama (bargaining).
The text emphasizes that in murābaḥa, the first price must be known.
4
Identify the conditions for bindingness (luzūm)
Freedom from the four famous options (khiyār al-majlis, khiyār al-sharṭ, etc.) and additional options like khiyār al-ghubn (deception) and khiyār al-ʿayb (defect).
Bindingness arises only when no party has a right to cancel.

المستهلكة بالنسيئة أنه يبيعها بثوب ويقبض الثوب ثم يبيعه بدراهم إلى أجل أقول وتجري هذه الحيلة في الصلح أيضاً. وقد صارت جملة الشرائط ستة وسبعين فشرائط الانعقاد أحد عشر، وشرائط النفاذ اثنان، وشرائط الصحة البدلين لكل منهما في بدل، وهو في اللغة القوة والقدرة، وشرعاً ما قدمناه والتابع وجوب تسليم المبيع والثمن ووجوب استبراء الجارية على المشتري وملك الاستمتاع بالجارية وثبوت الشفعة لو كان عقاراً وعتق المبيع لو كان محرماً من البائع. وأما صفة ذلك الحكم فاللزوم عند عدم خيار فليس لأحدهما فسخه فالبيع عند عدم الخيار من العقود اللازمة والعقود ثلاثة لازم من الطرفين وهو البيع والسلم والإجارة - وإن قلنا بفسخها بالأعذار - والصلح والحوالة والمساقاة والوصية بعد القبول بعد موت الموصي والنكاح والصداق والصدقة المقبوضة والهبة المقبوضة إذا وجد مانع من الموانع السبعة الآتية. ولازم من أحد الجانبين وهو الرهن فإنه لازم من جهة الراهن بعد التسليم دون المرتهن وجائز من الطرفين فلكل منهما فسخه وهو الشركة والوكالة والعارية لغير الراهن والمضاربة والوديعة والقضاء والوصاية قبل قبول الوصي، وأما بعده فلازمة والوصية قبل موت الموصي. وأما أنواعه فبالنظر إلى مطلق البيع أربعة : نافذ وموقوف وفاسد وباطل . فالنافذ ما أفاد الحكم للحال والموقوف ما أفاده عند الإجازة، والفاسد ما أفاده عند القبض، والباطل ما لم يفده أصلاً؛ كذا في الحاوي وغيره وهو ظاهر في أن الموقوف ليس من الفاسد وإنما هو إما من قسم الصحيح أو قسم برأسه وهو ظاهر كلامهم وبالنظر إلى المبيع أربعة : مقايضة وهي بيع العين بالعين وبيع الدين بالدين وهو الصرف وبيع الدين بالعين وهو السلم وعكسه وهو بيع العين بالدين كأكثر البياعات وبالنظر إلى الثمن خمسة: مرابحة وتولية وإشراك ووضيعة ومساومة. وستأتي البيوع المكروهة. وأما محاسنه فمنها التوصل إلى الأغراض وإخلاء العالم عن الفساد. وفي آخر بيوع البزازية قيل للإمام محمد : ألا تصنف في الزهد ؟ قال : حسبكم كتاب البيوع وكان التجار في القديم إذا سافروا استصحبوا معهم بد للتاجر من فقيه صديق اهـ. قال الشمني فقيهاً يرجعون إليه . أئمة . وعن خوارزم أنه لا وهي واقعة الفتوى ويكثر وقوع ذلك فاستفده .اهـ. قوله : (ستة وسبعين) فيه نظر لأن شرائط الانعقاد والنفاد والصحة ثمانية وثلاثون وشرائط اللزوم هذه المذكورات مع زيادة الخلو من الخيارات فصارت سبعة وسبعين، لكن علمت أن الصواب أن شرائط الانعقاد تسعة فيسقط منها اثنان، ومن شرائط الصحة اثنان أيضاً، ومن شرائط اللزوم أربعة فتبقى الجملة تسعة وستين. قوله : (والكل من غير تداخل ثمانية) لم يظهر لي مراده فتأمل. قوله : (لو كان محرماً من البائع) صوابه من المشتري .
Book of Sale. And from it is the condition of a temporary option known in addition to three, and from it is the exclusion of the slave-girl's pregnancy, and from it is consent, so the sale of the coerced person is corrupt and his purchase, and likewise the sale of talji'ah, and the first owns by possession but not the second. And from it is the benefit: selling what has no benefit and buying it is corrupt, so selling a dirham for a dirham equal in weight and quality is corrupt; as in al-Dhakhirah. As for the specific ones: from them is the knowledge of the term in a sale with a deferred price, so it is corrupt if unknown; and from them is possession in the buyer's sale of movables and in debt, so selling debt before taking possession is corrupt like the salam capital, even after annulment; and selling something for the debt owed by so-and-so, unlike if it is upon the seller. And from them is that the countervalue be specified in one of the two types of exchange, which is verbal; if silent about it, it is corrupt and ownership by possession; if denied, it is said corrupt and said void, so no ownership by possession. In al-Tatimmah: he sold it for a debt upon him while both know it is upon him, it is not valid. And from them is equality between the two countervalues in ribawi goods, and its detail will come in its chapter. And from them is freedom from suspicion of riba, and from them is the existence of the conditions of salam to come, and from them is possession in exchange before separation, and from them is that the first price be known in murabahah, tawliyah, ishrak, and wadi'ah sales. As for conditions of bindingness after conclusion and validity: freedom from the four well-known options, and added is option of quantity, option of deception if there is misrepresentation, option of entitlement of part of the sale item, option of treachery in murabahah, option of payment of price or its absence, option of investigation, option of loss of a desirable attribute, option of ratification of the unauthorized sale, option of destruction of part of the sale item—so there are three: valid not concluded because what is not valid from it is like corrupt, and other than it like void. And in his saying 'concluded valid' there is consideration, for the sale of the coerced is among the corrupt as he stated, and it is concluded but suspended...
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqā'iq, provides a comprehensive enumeration of the conditions (shurūṭ) of a valid sale (bay') according to the Hanafī school. The author begins by listing conditions that belong to the 'general' category, such as the requirement of an option (khiyār) for a known period not exceeding three days, the exclusion of the slave-girl's pregnancy from the sale (istithnā' ḥaml al-jāriyah), and the necessity of mutual consent (riḍā), explaining that a sale under coercion (mukrah) is fāsid (corrupt). He then distinguishes between conditions for validity (ṣiḥḥa) and bindingness (luzūm). For validity, he mentions knowledge of the term in a deferred sale, taking possession (qabḍ) before resale of movables, avoidance of debt-for-debt sale (bay' al-kālī' bi al-kālī'), specification of the countervalue, equality in ribawī goods, freedom from ribā suspicion, conditions of salam, and possession before separation in ṣarf. For bindingness, he lists freedom from the four famous options and additional options like khiyār al-ghubn (fraud) and khiyār al-'ayb (defect). The passage then discusses the classification of sales into nāfidh (effective), mawqūf (suspended), fāsid (corrupt), and bāṭil (void), explaining that a corrupt sale conveys ownership upon possession while a void one does not. It also categorizes sales by countervalue: muqāyaḍah (exchange), ṣarf (money exchange), salam, and ordinary sale. The author critiques the count of conditions (76 vs. 69) and ends with a narration about Imam Muhammad's emphasis on the book of sales. The commentary follows the structure: first general conditions, then specific ones for validity, then bindingness, then classifications, then a note on the count. Key Hanafī positions such as the sale of the coerced being fāsid and mawqūf (suspended) are highlighted.

Key Terms
نافذ (nāfidh): A sale that is fully effective immediately.
موقوف (mawqūf): A sale that is concluded but its effectiveness depends on subsequent ratification (ijāzah).
فاسد (fāsid): A sale that is concluded but defective; it conveys ownership upon possession.
باطل (bāṭil): A sale that fails to meet any condition of conclusion; it does not transfer ownership at all.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of sale conveys its ruling only upon possession (qabḍ)?
A) Nāfidh
B) Mawqūf
C) Fāsid
D) Bāṭil

Key Takeaway
Sales are classified by effect: nāfidh (immediate), mawqūf (suspended), fāsid (by possession), bāṭil (never), with bindingness requiring absence of options.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

The Conditions and Types of Sale in Hanafi Fiqh
Enumerates conditions, rulings, and classifications of sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four categories of sale conditions and classify contracts as binding from both sides, binding from one side, or revocable from both sides according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Sale conditions have four categories; its bindingness depends on absence of options; contracts are three types and sales four by effect.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the complete skeleton of the Hanafi law of sale. It first summarizes the conditions, then explains the legal rulings and subsidiary effects, then classifies contracts by their binding nature, and finally categorizes sales by effect, object, and price. Understanding these categories gives you the foundational taxonomy for all later fiqh of transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four condition categories
The commentator states that conditions of sale are divided into four sets: conditions of formation (inqi`ad), execution (nafadh), validity (sihhah), and bindingness (luzum). Note the initial count of 76 and the subsequent correction.
The counts are debated; focus on the categories, not the exact numbers.
2
Separate primary and subsidiary rulings
The primary ruling of sale is ownership (tamlik) of the two substitutes for each party. Subsidiary rulings include obligation to deliver, istibra' of a slave-girl, pre-emption, etc. Distinguish which effects are intrinsic (primary) and which are attached (subsidiary).
The text also corrects a phrase: 'mahram from the seller' should be 'mahram from the buyer'.
3
Classify contracts by bindingness
Contracts are of three types: laazim min al-tarafayn (binding on both parties), laazim min ahad al-janibayn (binding on one side only, e.g., rahn), and ja'iz min al-tarafayn (revocable by either party). List the examples given for each.
Note that ijarah is considered laazim even though it can be rescinded due to excuses.
4
Categorize sales by effect, object, and price
By effect: nafidh (effective immediately), mawquf (suspended pending authorization), fasid (corrupt, becomes effective upon possession), batil (void). By object: muqayadah, sarf, salam, and ordinary sale. By price: murabahah, tawliyah, ishrak, wadi`ah, musawamah.
The commentator clarifies that mawquf is not a type of fasid; it is either sahih or a separate category.
5
Note the virtue and the correction
The passage ends with Imam Muhammad's praise of fiqh of sales and a textual correction about the count. Recognize that the author is engaging in critical commentary (sharh) on earlier matn.
This highlights the importance of scholarly verification in the Hanafi tradition.

كتاب البيع 6 عشر. وقد صارت جملة الشرائط ستة وسبعين فشرائط الانعقاد أحد عشر، وشرائط النفاذ اثنان، وشرائط الصحة خمسة وعشرون وشرط اللزوم واحد بعد اجتماع الكل، فعلى هذا شرائط اللزوم تسعة وثلاثون، والكل من غير تداخل ثمانية وسبب شرعيته تعلق البقاء المعلوم فيه الله تعالى على وجه جميل. وأما أحكامه فالأصلي له الملك في البدلين لكل منهما في بدل، وهو في اللغة القوة والقدرة، وشرعاً ما قدمناه والتابع وجوب تسليم المبيع والثمن ووجوب استبراء الجارية على المشتري وملك الاستمتاع بالجارية وثبوت الشفعة لو كان عقاراً وعتق المبيع لو كان محرماً من البائع. وأما صفة ذلك الحكم فاللزوم عند عدم خيار فليس لأحدهما فسخه فالبيع عند عدم الخيار من العقود اللازمة والعقود ثلاثة لازم من الطرفين وهو البيع والسلم والإجارة - Book of Sale... Sixteen. And indeed the total conditions have become seventy-six: conditions of formation are eleven, conditions of execution are two, conditions of validity are twenty-five, and one condition of bindingness after the meeting of all. Thus, the conditions of bindingness are thirty-nine, and all without overlapping are eight. And the reason for its legality is the attachment of known subsistence to Allah on a beautiful manner. As for its rulings, the primary is ownership in the two substitutes for each of them in a substitute, and it is in language strength and ability, and legally what we have presented. And the subsidiary: obligation to deliver the sold item and the price, obligation of istibra' of the slave-girl upon the buyer, ownership of enjoyment of the slave-girl, establishment of pre-emption if it is real estate, and emancipation of the sold item if it was a mahram from the seller. As for the quality of that ruling, it is bindingness in the absence of an option, so neither of them may rescind it. Thus sale without option is among binding contracts. And contracts are three: binding from both sides - and that is sale, salam, ijarah (even though we say it can be rescinded due to excuses), sulh, hawalah, musaqah, wasiyyah after acceptance after the testator's death, nikah, sadaq, accepted sadaqah, and accepted gift if a preventer from the seven preventers exists; binding from one side - and that is rahn, for it is binding from the side of the rahin after delivery but not the murtahin; and revocable from both sides - and each may rescind it, and that is shirkah, wakalah, ariyah (other than rahn), mudarabah, wadi'ah, qada', and wasayah before the executor's acceptance, but after it becomes binding, and wasiyyah before the testator's death. As for its types, with respect to absolute sale there are four: effective, suspended, corrupt, and void. The effective is that which gives the ruling immediately; the suspended is that which gives it upon authorization; the corrupt is that which gives it upon possession; and the void is that which does not give it at all. Thus in al-Hawi and others, and it is apparent that the suspended is not corrupt; rather it is either of the sound type or a category on its own, and this is apparent from their statements. And with respect to the sold item, four: exchange (which is sale of commodity for commodity), sale of debt for debt (which is sarf), sale of debt for commodity (which is salam), and its opposite which is sale of commodity for debt (like most sales). And with respect to the price, five: murabahah, tawliyah, ishrak, wadi'ah, and musawamah. And the disliked sales will come. As for its benefits, among them are achieving goals and cleansing the world from corruption. And at the end of Buyu' al-Bazzaziyyah, it was said to Imam Muhammad: 'Will you not write on asceticism?' He said: 'The book of sales is sufficient for you.' And the merchants in the past, when they traveled, they used to take with them... a need for the merchant of a jurist friend. End. Al-Shumnunni said: 'Jurists they refer to. Imams.' And from Khwarazm that there is no... and it is a fatwa occurrence and it occurs frequently, so benefit from it. End. His statement: 'Seventy-six' - there is consideration, because the conditions of formation, execution, and validity are thirty-eight, and the conditions of bindingness mentioned here with the addition of freedom from options become seventy-seven, but you know that the correct is that the conditions of formation are nine, so two drop from them, and from the conditions of validity also two, and from the conditions of bindingness four, so the total remains sixty-nine. His statement: 'And all without overlapping eight' - I did not understand his intent, so contemplate. His statement: 'If the sold item was a mahram from the seller' - the correct is 'from the buyer'.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It opens by summarizing the conditions of sale, first giving a count of seventy-six conditions, then breaking them down: eleven for formation (inqi`ad), two for execution (nafadh), twenty-five for validity (sihhah), and one for bindingness (luzum) after all conditions are met, resulting in thirty-nine conditions for bindingness. The author notes that without overlap, the total is eight (meaning distinct categories). He then explains the primary ruling of sale: ownership of the two substitutes for each party. Next, he lists subsidiary rulings: delivery, istibra' of a slave-girl, enjoyment of a slave-girl, preemption for real estate, and emancipation if a mahram relative is sold (correcting that the mahram relation is to the buyer, not seller). He classifies contracts into three types: binding from both sides (e.g., sale, salam, ijarah, sulh, hawalah, etc.), binding from one side (rahn), and revocable from both sides (e.g., shirkah, wakalah, ariyah). Then he categorizes types of sale by different criteria: by effect (nafidh, mawquf, fasid, batil), by the object (muqayadah, sarf, salam, and normal sale), and by price (murabahah, tawliyah, ishrak, wadi`ah, musawamah). Finally, he mentions the virtues of trade, quoting Imam Muhammad's saying that the book of sales suffices for asceticism. The passage ends with annotations correcting the count and a textual correction.

Key Terms
شرائط الانعقاد (sharaait al-inqi`ad): Conditions for the contract to be formed (a`qd)
العقود اللازمة (al-`uquud al-laazimah): Contracts binding on both parties, cannot be rescinded unilaterally
البيع (al-bay`): Exchange of property for property with mutual consent

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many types of contracts are there in terms of bindingness?
A) Two: binding and revocable
B) Three: binding from both sides, binding from one side, revocable from both sides
C) Four: effective, suspended, corrupt, void
D) One: all contracts are binding

Key Takeaway
Sale conditions are partitioned into formation, execution, validity, and bindingness; contracts are classified by bindingness into three types, and sales by effect into four types: nafidh, mawquf, fasid, batil.

Evidence for the Legality of Sale in Hanafi Fiqh
Provides dalil for legality of sale from four sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sources of evidence for the legality of sale in the Hanafi school and explain why trade is considered the best earning after jihad.

Core Idea
Trade is legally permissible by Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma, and reason — and after jihad it is the best earning.

The Hanafi school establishes the permissibility of sale (al-bay') on multiple authoritative proofs. In this passage, the commentator cites the personal conduct of the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions, then summarizes the four classical sources: the Qur'an, the Sunnah, consensus (ijma), and rational necessity. Understanding these proofs strengthens your grasp of Hanafi legal methodology in commercial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sale/trade (tijarah). It is originally mubah (permissible) but can change based on circumstances.
Hanafis classify trade as mubah, but it may become wajib (e.g., fard kifayah) if the community lacks traders.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The passage lists four sources: the Book (Qur'an), the Sunnah, Ijma (consensus), and rational proof (al-ma'qul). The Qur'anic basis is the general permission from verses like 2:275.
The specific verse is not quoted, but it is referenced by name.
3
Examine the historical precedent
The Prophet ﷺ traded for Khadija before prophethood, and major Companions (Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Abbas) were traders in various goods. This proves practice (Sunnah) and tacit approval.
The timing (before prophethood) shows trade is human and permissible for all.
4
Analyze the Hanafi ranking
After jihad, trade is the best earning, then agriculture, then craftsmanship. This ranking is derived from the Prophet's example and scholarly deduction.
This is a distinctive Hanafi view; other schools may not rank them.
5
Conclude the legal implication
The multiple proofs establish that sale is fundamentally lawful and virtuous. Any prohibition is an exception (e.g., riba, gharar).
This aligns with the principle that all contracts are permissible unless prohibited.

رحمه الله تعالى : وقد صح عند أصحاب السير أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أتجر لخديجة رضي الله تعالى عنها لكن قبل البعثة بخمسة عشر سنة فإنه بعث على رأس الأربعين وخرج تاجراً إلى الشام لخديجة رضي الله تعالى عنها لما بلغ خمساً وعشرين سنة قبل أن يتزوجها بشهرين وخمسة وعشرين يوماً، وكان أبو بكر رضي الله تعالى عنه تاجراً في البز، وكان عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه في الطعام، وعثمان رضي الله تعالى عنه في التمر والبز، وعباس رضي الله عنه في العطر، ومن هنا قال أصحابنا : أفضل الكسب بعد الجهاد التجارة ثم الحراثة ثم الصناعة اهـ. وأما دليله فالكتاب والسنة والإجماع والمعقول وهو العاشر من مواضعه
May Allah have mercy on him: It has been established in the books of biographies that the Prophet peace be upon him traded for Khadija may Allah be pleased with her, but fifteen years before the prophethood, for he was sent at the beginning of forty, and he went out as a trader to Syria for Khadija may Allah be pleased with her when he reached twenty-five years, two months and twenty-five days before he married her. And Abu Bakr may Allah be pleased with him was a trader in cloth; Umar may Allah be pleased with him was in food; Uthman may Allah be pleased with him was in dates and cloth; and Abbas may Allah be pleased with him was in perfume. From here our scholars said: The best earning after jihad is trade, then cultivation, then craftsmanship. End. As for its evidence, it is the Book, the Sunnah, consensus, and rational proof, and it is the tenth of its topics.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage provides the evidence (dalil) for the legality of sale and trade. The author begins with historical examples: the Prophet himself engaged in trade for Khadija before prophethood, and the major companions (Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Abbas) were traders in various goods. From this, the Hanafi scholars concluded that after jihad, trade is the best means of earning, followed by agriculture and then craftsmanship. The text then states the four sources of evidence: the Qur'an (e.g., verse 2:275 'Allah has permitted trade'), the Sunnah (prophetic practice and sayings), consensus (ijma) of the ummah on the permissibility, and rational proof (al-ma`qul) – meaning that trade is a natural human need. This passage functions as a proof statement (ruling_with_proof) within the larger commentary.

Key Terms
أصحاب السير (ashab al-siyar): Authors of biographical works (sirah) about the Prophet
أفضل الكسب (afdal al-kasb): The best means of earning a livelihood

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the best earning after jihad according to Hanafi scholars?
A) Agriculture
B) Trade
C) Craftsmanship
D) All are equal

Key Takeaway
Sale is legally permissible by multiple proofs (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma, reason), and after jihad it is the most virtuous earning in the Hanafi school.

Selling at a Grossly Unequal Price: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on selling an item worth a dirham for a thousand dirhams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the validity of a sale with extreme price disparity and identify the authority level (nawadir) of the transmitted ruling.

Core Idea
A sale with extreme price disparity is valid but disliked (makruh) according to Imam Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf considers it valid — and this ruling comes from rare transmissions, not the core usul.

This passage from Khizanat al-Fatawa presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on selling an item worth one dirham for a thousand dirhams. Although such a transaction involves extreme imbalance in value, the Hanafi school does not automatically void it. The key question is whether the gross disparity makes the sale invalid or merely disliked, and the authority of the ruling is from rare narrations (nawadir), not the well-known usul.

Guided Path
1
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify that the passage is a far' (branch) from Khizanat al-Fatawa, citing a sale of a one-dirham item for a thousand dirhams. Note the phrase 'fee ghayr riwayat al-usul' indicating this is not from the core transmitted texts (Zahir al-Riwayah) but from rare transmissions (nawadir).
The authority weight is nawadir, meaning it is not the strongest position in the school.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf holds that the sale is valid (yajuz) and not binding (la yalzam). Understand 'la yalzam' as meaning the ruling is not obligatory or perhaps the seller is not forced to complete the sale? The text is brief; later scholars interpret it as a valid but non-binding transaction.
The exact implication of 'not binding' is debated; some say it means the ruling is not from the usul and thus not binding to follow.
3
State Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad rules that such a sale is disliked (makruh). This is makruh tanzihi (better to avoid but not sinful), reflecting caution against gross imbalance.
Muhammad's view is generally preferred in later fatwa practice due to the principle of avoiding ghubn fahish (gross fraud).
4
Analyze the authority weight
Because the ruling is not in the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, it is considered nawadir. The text does not give tarjih, but later Hanafi muftis lean towards Muhammad's position (makruh) as the cautious approach.
The phrase 'fee ghayr riwayat al-usul' serves as a disclaimer: this is not the strongest transmission.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If one follows Abu Yusuf, the sale is valid and enforceable, but not strongly recommended. If one follows Muhammad, the sale is valid yet disliked; the parties are advised not to enter such a transaction. The mufta bihi today is that it is makruh.
This dispute does not affect the basic validity of the contract but its desirability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(فرع حسن) من خزانة الفتاوى ما يساوي درهماً بألف درهم في غير رواية الأصول يجوز ولا يلزم في قول أبي يوسف بيع وقال محمد يكره .اهـ.
(A good branch) from Khizanat al-Fatawa: What equals a dirham sold for a thousand dirhams – in other than the riwayah of the usul, it is permitted and not binding, according to Abu Yusuf it is a sale, and Muhammad said it is disliked. End.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This short passage from `Khizanat al-Fatawa` presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The issue: selling an item worth one dirham for a thousand dirhams (a grossly unequal price). According to Abu Yusuf, this is a valid sale (yajuz) and not binding (la yalzam) – meaning the seller cannot force the buyer to take it? Or it means the ruling is not from the usul? The text says 'fee ghayr riwayat al-usul' – i.e., this is not from the well-known transmitted narrations (the usul of Imam Muhammad), indicating it is a rare transmission (nawadir). Muhammad al-Shaybani said it is disliked (makruh). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is likely that it is valid but disliked, following Muhammad's view. The passage is a complete ruling with ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
خزانة الفتاوى (khizanat al-fatawa): A collection of fatwas by a later Hanafi scholar
رواية الأصول (riwayat al-usul): The well-known transmitted narrations (the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah)
يكره (yukrah): Disliked (makruh tanzihi), meaning better to avoid but not sinful

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Valid but not binding
C) Disliked (makruh)
D) Void

Key Takeaway
A sale with extreme price disparity is valid but disliked (makruh) according to the preferred Hanafi view, and this ruling comes from rare transmissions, not the core usul.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

The Pillars of Sale: Offer, Acceptance, and the Legal Link
Defines sale and explains its pillars and legal nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sale, identify its three pillars, and explain why the legal link (irtibat) is considered a distinct element.

Core Idea
Sale is a composite of offer, acceptance, and the legal bond between them — not merely the resulting ownership.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author unpacks the definition of sale from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: 'Sale is binding by offer and acceptance.' He examines two competing views within the Hanafi school: one that reduces sale to the resulting ruling of ownership, and another that sees it as a composite of offer, acceptance, and a legal link (irtibat). The author adopts the composite view, explaining why the third element is necessary for a complete legal definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core statement
The matn says 'Sale is binding by offer and acceptance.' What does this imply about the nature of sale? Does it mean sale itself is the combination of the two utterances, or something else?
2
Understand the two positions
One view (from Fath al-Qadir) says sale is merely the ruling (ownership) that results from offer and acceptance; there is no third element. The other view says sale is the sum of offer, acceptance, and the legal link that ties them.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq sides with the composite view.
3
Analyze the reasoning for the composite view
If sale were only the ruling, then the phrase 'sale is concluded by offer and acceptance' would be circular (the ruling is concluded by its cause). Instead, sale as a contract must be a third entity that is 'concluded' by the two utterances. This third entity is the legal link.
See references to al-`Inayah and al-Binayah.
4
Recognize the Hanafi tarjih
The author, following al-`Inayah and al-Binayah, establishes the composite view as the relied-upon position. This means sale in the Hanafi school is defined as the combination of offer, acceptance, and the legal link.
The birthing of the contract is the creation of this legal link.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع
رحمه الله تعالى : وقد صح عند أصحاب السير أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أتجر لخديجة رضي الله تعالى عنها لكن قبل البعثة بخمسة عشر سنة فإنه بعث على رأس الأربعين وخرج تاجراً إلى الشام لخديجة رضي الله تعالى عنها لما بلغ خمساً وعشرين سنة قبل أن يتزوجها بشهرين وخمسة وعشرين يوماً، وكان أبو بكر رضي الله تعالى عنه تاجراً في البز، وكان عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه في الطعام، وعثمان رضي الله تعالى عنه في التمر والبز، وعباس رضي الله عنه في العطر، ومن هنا قال أصحابنا : أفضل الكسب بعد الجهاد التجارة ثم الحراثة ثم الصناعة اهـ. وأما دليله فالكتاب والسنة والإجماع والمعقول وهو العاشر من مواضعه (فرع حسن) من خزانة الفتاوى للآخر على وجه يظهر أثره في المحل .اهـ. وهو أمر ثالث غير الإيجاب والقبول والبيع مجموع الثلاثة فصح التركيب. وفي شرح الوقاية من كتاب النكاح : فالعقد ربط أجزاء التصرف أي الإيجاب والقبول شرعاً لكن هنا أريد بالعقد الحاصل بالمصدر وهو الارتباط لكن النكاح الإيجاب والقبول مع ذلك الارتباط وإنما قلنا هذا لأن الشرع يعتبر الإيجاب والقبول أركان عقد النكاح لا أموراً خارجية كالشرائط ونحوها، وقد ذكرت في شرح التنقيح للبيع، والإيجاب والقبول والتعاطي علة مادية والمبادلة تكون بين اثنين فهي العلة الفاعلية وسكت العلة الغائية هنا وذكرها في النكاح وهي هنا الملك وثمة المصالح المتعلقة بالنكاح، وذكر عن الشمني أن المعنى أنه (وقد يقال لا حاجة إلى هذا التكلف) أي بحيث يعسر ولا كتاب البيع والعهد والبيع فانعقد .اهـ. فإن قلت : فما معنى قولهم البيع ينعقد وكذا أمثاله فإن المعنى العقد ينعقد؟ قلت : المعنى العقد الشرعي الخاص يثبت بالإيجاب والقبول. وفي القاموس : عقد الحبل والبيع والعهد يعقده شده. وفي تفسير الفخر الرازي: العقد وصل الشيء بالشيء على سبيل الاستثبات والاستحكام .اهـ. وفي تفسير القاضي : وأصل العقد الجمع بين الشيئين الانفصال بينهما .اهـ. والعقد شرعاً على ما في التوضيح ربط القبول بالإيجاب . وأما حمل كلام المستصفى على الحكم الذي هو الملك فليس بظاهر لأنه قال : البيع عبارة عن أثر شرعي يظهر في المحل عند الإيجاب والقبول حتى يكون العاقد قادراً على التصرف اهـ . يصح حمله عليه لأن الحكم لا يظهر عندهما إنما يظهر بهما عقيبهما لأن حكم الشيء يعقبه، ولأنه جعل القدرة على التصرف غاية لذلك الأثر والقدرة هي الملك فلا يصح أن يراد بذلك الأثر الملك لأن المغيا غير الغاية فافهم هذا التقرير فإنه دقيق. والإيجاب لغة الالتزام والإثبات، وفي الفقه في المعاملات ما يذكر أوّلاً من كلام المتعاقدين الدال على الرضا، وسمي به لأنه يثبت خيار القبول للآخر، وسواء وقع من البائع كبعت، أو من المشتري كأن يبدأ المشتري. والقبول في اللغة من قبلت العقد أقبله - من باب تعب ـ قبولاً بالفتح، والضم لغة حكاها ابن الإعرابي ؛ كذا في المصباح. وفي الفقه : اللفظ الصادر ثانياً الواقع جواباً قبولاً؛ سمي ؛ هكذا عرفه الجمهور وخالفهم في فتح القدير فعرفه بأنه الفعل الصادر ثانياً قال : وإنما قلنا بأنه الفعل الأعم منه ومن القبول فإن من الفروع ما لو قال كل فأكله هذا الطعام بدرهم تم البيع وأكله حلال والركوب واللبس بعد قول البائع اركبها بمائة وألبسه بكذا رضاً بالبيع، وكذا إذا قال بعته بألف فقبضه ولم يقل شيئاً كان قبضه قبولاً بخلاف بيع التعاطي فإنه ليس فيه إيجاب بل قبض بعد معرفة الثمن فقط، ففي جعل مسألة القبض بعد قوله بعتك بألف من صور التعاطي كما فعل بعضهم أي في غاية البيان نظر كما لا يخفى اهـ. ولا حاجة إلى تغيير كلام القوم وما ذكره من الفروع إنما هو من باب أن القبول يقوم مقامه فعل ولهذا قال في الخانية : يقوم القبض مقام القبول وفي التتارخانية : اشتريت طعامك هذا بألف فتصدق به ففعل في المجلس ولم يتكلم جاز وإن تفرقا لا. وقيد اللزوم بالإيجاب والقبول للإشارة إلى أن البائع إذا باع وقبل المشتري لا يحتاج بعدهما إلى إحازة البائع. قال في الذخيرة ذكر محمد بن الحسن رحمه الله تعالى في كتاب الوكالة مسألة تدل تقدير المضاف قبل البيع وهو لفظ حكم ومراده الرد على الفتح ، ثم إن قوله «لأن الانعقاد الخ» إنما يظهر على عبارة الهداية حيث عبر فيها بـ ينعقد بدل قول المصنف يلزم وفرق ما بينهما. ثم إن ما بنى عليه كلامه من أن البيع مجموع الإيجاب والقبول مع الارتباط لا يفيد لأن المعنى يصير البيع الذي هو مجموع الثلاثة ينعقد بالإيجاب والقبول أي يرتبط نعم يتضح تفسير ينعقد بيحصل تأمل.
Book of Sale: May Allah have mercy on him: It is authentically reported from the chroniclers that the Prophet (peace be upon him) traded for Khadijah (may Allah be pleased with her) fifteen years before the prophethood, for he was sent at forty years of age and went as a merchant to Syria for Khadijah at age twenty-five, two months and twenty-five days before marrying her. Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) was a cloth merchant, Umar was in food, Uthman in dates and cloth, and Abbas in perfume. Hence our companions said: The best earning after jihad is trade, then agriculture, then craftsmanship. As for its proof: the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and reason. And it is the tenth of its topics. (A good branch) from Khizanat al-Fatawa: What is equal to one dirham with a thousand dirhams is permissible in other than the sound narration, and according to Abu Yusuf it is a sale, and Muhammad said it is disliked. His saying: (Sale is binding by offer and acceptance) means the ruling of sale is binding by them, because he made them other than it, and that it is binding by them even though sale is nothing but them because they are its pillars as we have verified. And what is said that it is a meaning as we have presented is nothing but the ruling. So what is realized from the Law is only the establishment of the known ruling of exchange of ownership upon the occurrence of the two acts, namely the two parts, by placing them as a cause for it legally, and there is no third thing here; as verified in Fath al-Qadir. It may be said: There is no need for this complication, because the speech is correct without it, since the conclusion (al-in'iqaad) – as in al-`Inayah – is the attachment of the speech of one contracting party to the other legally. And in al-Binayah it is the joining of the speech of one to the other in a manner that shows its effect on the subject. It is a third thing besides offer and acceptance, and sale is the sum of the three, so the composition is correct. In Sharh al-Wiqayah from the Book of Marriage: The contract is the tying of the parts of the transaction, i.e., offer and acceptance, legally. But here what is meant by the contract obtained from the verbal noun is the connection, but marriage is offer and acceptance with that connection. We only say this because the Law considers offer and acceptance as pillars of the marriage contract, not external matters like conditions. And it was mentioned in Sharh al-Tanqih in the chapter of prohibition: Like sale, for the Law rules that the sensibly existing offer and acceptance are linked by a legal link, so a legal meaning occurs which is the ownership of the buyer as its effect. That meaning is the legal sale. What is meant by that meaning is the composite of offer and acceptance with that link. For some mistakenly thought that sale is merely that legal meaning and that offer and acceptance are its instruments, because them being pillars contradicts that. It is a good explanation. And in the Book of Sale: Exchange is the formal cause of sale, and offer, acceptance, and mutual giving are the material cause. Exchange occurs between two, so it is the efficient cause, and the final cause is omitted here, mentioned in marriage, which is ownership, and there the interests related to marriage. He mentioned from al-Shumnuni that the meaning is that it is concluded by the combination of offer and acceptance. In al-Qamus: I tied the rope... His saying: (Because he) meaning the author made them, i.e., offer and acceptance, other than it, i.e., other than sale. His saying: (And what is said that it is a legal meaning) its author is the author in al-Mustasfa as previously. His saying: (It may be said there is no need for this complication) meaning it is difficult and not needed... Book of Sale, and the rope, and the sale, so it is concluded. If you say: What is the meaning of their statement “the sale is concluded” and the like, for the meaning is the contract is concluded? I say: The meaning is the specific legal contract is established by offer and acceptance. In al-Qamus: He tied the rope, the sale, and the covenant, he tied it, meaning he tightened it. In Tafsir al-Razi: The contract is connecting something to something in a firm and strong manner. In the Qadi’s Tafsir: The origin of contract is the joining of two things with a separation between them. The contract legally, according to what is in al-Tawdih, is the binding of acceptance to offer. As for interpreting the statement of al-Mustasfa as the ruling which is ownership, it is not apparent because he said: Sale is an expression of a legal effect that appears in the subject upon offer and acceptance so that the contracting party is able to dispose. It is possible to interpret it as such because the ruling does not appear at them but rather by them after them, because the ruling of a thing follows it, and because he made the ability to dispose as the end of that effect, and ability is ownership, so it is not correct to mean by that effect ownership because the thing made the goal is not the goal itself. Understand this explanation for it is subtle. Offer (ijab) linguistically means commitment and affirmation, and in fiqh of transactions it is what is mentioned first from the speech of the two contracting parties indicating consent, and it is named so because it establishes the option of acceptance for the other, whether it comes from the seller like “I sold” or from the buyer like the buyer initiating. Acceptance (qabul) linguistically from “I accepted the contract, I accept it” from the paradigm of ta`iba, acceptance with a fatha, and damma is a language reported by Ibn al-A`rabi; as in al-Misbah. In fiqh: the word uttered second that occurs as a response, called acceptance; this is the definition of the majority, but in Fath al-Qadir he differed and defined it as the action that occurs second. He said: We only say it is the action, general including acceptance, for among the branches is if one says “Eat” and he eats this food for a dirham, the sale is completed and eating it is permissible, and riding and wearing after the seller says “Ride it for a hundred” and “Dress him for such” is consent to the sale. Similarly, if he says “I sold it to you for a thousand” and he takes possession without saying anything, his taking possession is acceptance, unlike the sale of mu`atah (mutual giving) which has no offer but only taking possession after knowing the price. So considering the case of taking possession after his saying “I sold it to you for a thousand” as a form of mu`atah as some have done is subject to scrutiny. There is no need to change the statement of the scholars, and what he mentioned of branches is only from the angle that an action stands in place of acceptance, hence in al-Khaniyyah: Taking possession stands in place of acceptance. In al-Tatar Khaniyyah: If one says “I bought this food of yours for a thousand” and he gives it in charity and does so in the session without speaking, it is valid; if they separate, no. The restriction of bindingness by offer and acceptance indicates that when the seller sells and the buyer accepts, there is no need thereafter for the seller's permission. In al-Dhakhirah: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan mentioned a case in the Book of Agency that indicates the estimation of an omitted word before the word “sale” which is the word “ruling”, and his intent is to refute Fath. Then his statement “because the conclusion etc.” only appears in the phrasing of al-Hidayah where he used “concludes” instead of the author's “is binding”, and there is a difference between them. Moreover, what he based his statement on that sale is the sum of offer and acceptance with the link does not benefit, because the meaning becomes that sale which is the sum of the three is concluded by offer and acceptance, i.e., it ties together. Yes, the interpretation of “concludes” as “occurs” becomes clear after reflection.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq: 'Sale is binding by offer and acceptance.' It begins with a brief historical context about the Prophet's own trading before prophethood and the trade of the Companions, establishing the virtue of trade. The core of the passage is a detailed legal discussion on the definition of sale (bay'). The author examines two main views: (1) Sale is merely the ruling (hukm) of ownership that results from offer and acceptance, as posited by some scholars including the author of Kanz. (2) Sale is a composite of offer, acceptance, and the legal link (irtibat) between them, which is a third element. The author sides with the second view, citing authorities like al-`Inayah and al-Binayah. He argues that if sale were only the ruling, then the phrase 'sale is concluded by offer and acceptance' would be problematic because it would mean 'the ruling is concluded by the cause', which is circular. Instead, the correct understanding is that the legal contract (al-`aqd al-shar`i) is a separate entity established by offer and acceptance, and sale is the name for the combination of these three: offer, acceptance, and the legal link. The passage also provides linguistic definitions of 'ijab' and 'qabul' and discusses cases where actions replace verbal acceptance, such as taking possession. The author concludes by clarifying that the restriction of bindingness (luzum) by offer and acceptance means that once both are exchanged, no further action (like the seller's permission) is needed. This lesson is essential for understanding the fundamental nature of contracts in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
البيع (al-bay'): A legal contract (عقد) that transfers ownership of a commodity for a price, consisting of offer, acceptance, and the legal link between them.
الإيجاب (al-ijāb): The first utterance from either contracting party indicating consent, such as 'I sold' or 'I bought'.
القبول (al-qabūl): The second utterance (or action) that responds to and accepts the offer, such as 'I accept' or taking possession with intent.
العقد (al-‘aqd): The legal connection or tie between offer and acceptance, resulting in a binding contract.
الارتباط (al-irtibāṭ): The legal bond that links offer and acceptance, making them a single contractual entity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, which of the following is NOT a pillar of a valid sale (bay‘)?
A) Offer (ijab)
B) Acceptance (qabul)
C) Legal link (irtibat)
D) Delivery of goods

Key Takeaway
Sale in the Hanafi school is a composite contract consisting of offer, acceptance, and the legally recognized link between them.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Modes of Offer and Acceptance: Verbal and Non-Verbal
Explains the modalities of offer and acceptance, including action-based acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between verbal and non-verbal acceptance, and apply the Hanafi rules for when actions constitute valid acceptance in a sale.

Core Idea
Acceptance in a sale is not limited to words; an appropriate action with intent can also constitute valid acceptance in the Hanafi school.

After defining the pillars of sale, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into the linguistic and practical aspects of offer and acceptance. He provides detailed definitions of 'ijab' and 'qabul', and then explores cases where an action, such as taking possession, eating, or riding, can serve as acceptance. This lesson covers the Hanafi flexibility in the modes of contracting, including the controversial issue of mu'atah (mutual giving without verbal exchange).

Guided Path
1
Review the linguistic definitions
Ijab linguistically means commitment and affirmation. Qabul means acceptance. In legal terminology, ijab is the first speech indicating consent, and qabul is the response. The majority define qabul as the second utterance.
2
Understand the alternative definition from Fath al-Qadir
Fath al-Qadir defines qabul as 'the act that occurs second' — not limited to speech. This includes actions like taking possession, eating, or riding after an offer.
This expands the scope of valid acceptance beyond verbal utterances.
3
Apply to specific examples from the text
If a seller says 'Sell you this food for $5' and the buyer eats it, the sale is valid. Similarly, if the seller says 'Ride this horse for $100' and the buyer rides, it is acceptance. Taking possession after an offer also constitutes acceptance.
These cases show that actions can substitute for verbal qabul.
4
Distinguish mu'atah from these cases
Mu'atah (mutual giving) has no verbal offer; it is based solely on actions (e.g., taking an item and paying). In the examples above, there is a verbal offer followed by an action, which is different from pure mu'atah.
Some scholars treat cases with a verbal offer as part of mu'atah by extension, but the author notes this is subject to scrutiny.

يفيد لأن المعنى يصير البيع الذي هو مجموع الثلاثة ينعقد بالإيجاب والقبول أي يرتبط نعم يتضح تفسير ينعقد بيحصل تأمل.
Book of Sale: May Allah have mercy on him: It is authentically reported from the chroniclers that the Prophet (peace be upon him) traded for Khadijah (may Allah be pleased with her) fifteen years before the prophethood, for he was sent at forty years of age and went as a merchant to Syria for Khadijah at age twenty-five, two months and twenty-five days before marrying her. Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) was a cloth merchant, Umar was in food, Uthman in dates and cloth, and Abbas in perfume. Hence our companions said: The best earning after jihad is trade, then agriculture, then craftsmanship. As for its proof: the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and reason. And it is the tenth of its topics. (A good branch) from Khizanat al-Fatawa: What is equal to one dirham with a thousand dirhams is permissible in other than the sound narration, and according to Abu Yusuf it is a sale, and Muhammad said it is disliked. His saying: (Sale is binding by offer and acceptance) means the ruling of sale is binding by them, because he made them other than it, and that it is binding by them even though sale is nothing but them because they are its pillars as we have verified. And what is said that it is a meaning as we have presented is nothing but the ruling. So what is realized from the Law is only the establishment of the known ruling of exchange of ownership upon the occurrence of the two acts, namely the two parts, by placing them as a cause for it legally, and there is no third thing here; as verified in Fath al-Qadir. It may be said: There is no need for this complication, because the speech is correct without it, since the conclusion (al-in'iqaad) – as in al-`Inayah – is the attachment of the speech of one contracting party to the other legally. And in al-Binayah it is the joining of the speech of one to the other in a manner that shows its effect on the subject. It is a third thing besides offer and acceptance, and sale is the sum of the three, so the composition is correct. In Sharh al-Wiqayah from the Book of Marriage: The contract is the tying of the parts of the transaction, i.e., offer and acceptance, legally. But here what is meant by the contract obtained from the verbal noun is the connection, but marriage is offer and acceptance with that connection. We only say this because the Law considers offer and acceptance as pillars of the marriage contract, not external matters like conditions. And it was mentioned in Sharh al-Tanqih in the chapter of prohibition: Like sale, for the Law rules that the sensibly existing offer and acceptance are linked by a legal link, so a legal meaning occurs which is the ownership of the buyer as its effect. That meaning is the legal sale. What is meant by that meaning is the composite of offer and acceptance with that link. For some mistakenly thought that sale is merely that legal meaning and that offer and acceptance are its instruments, because them being pillars contradicts that. It is a good explanation. And in the Book of Sale: Exchange is the formal cause of sale, and offer, acceptance, and mutual giving are the material cause. Exchange occurs between two, so it is the efficient cause, and the final cause is omitted here, mentioned in marriage, which is ownership, and there the interests related to marriage. He mentioned from al-Shumnuni that the meaning is that it is concluded by the combination of offer and acceptance. In al-Qamus: I tied the rope... His saying: (Because he) meaning the author made them, i.e., offer and acceptance, other than it, i.e., other than sale. His saying: (And what is said that it is a legal meaning) its author is the author in al-Mustasfa as previously. His saying: (It may be said there is no need for this complication) meaning it is difficult and not needed... Book of Sale, and the rope, and the sale, so it is concluded. If you say: What is the meaning of their statement “the sale is concluded” and the like, for the meaning is the contract is concluded? I say: The meaning is the specific legal contract is established by offer and acceptance. In al-Qamus: He tied the rope, the sale, and the covenant, he tied it, meaning he tightened it. In Tafsir al-Razi: The contract is connecting something to something in a firm and strong manner. In the Qadi’s Tafsir: The origin of contract is the joining of two things with a separation between them. The contract legally, according to what is in al-Tawdih, is the binding of acceptance to offer. As for interpreting the statement of al-Mustasfa as the ruling which is ownership, it is not apparent because he said: Sale is an expression of a legal effect that appears in the subject upon offer and acceptance so that the contracting party is able to dispose. It is possible to interpret it as such because the ruling does not appear at them but rather by them after them, because the ruling of a thing follows it, and because he made the ability to dispose as the end of that effect, and ability is ownership, so it is not correct to mean by that effect ownership because the thing made the goal is not the goal itself. Understand this explanation for it is subtle. Offer (ijab) linguistically means commitment and affirmation, and in fiqh of transactions it is what is mentioned first from the speech of the two contracting parties indicating consent, and it is named so because it establishes the option of acceptance for the other, whether it comes from the seller like “I sold” or from the buyer like the buyer initiating. Acceptance (qabul) linguistically from “I accepted the contract, I accept it” from the paradigm of ta`iba, acceptance with a fatha, and damma is a language reported by Ibn al-A`rabi; as in al-Misbah. In fiqh: the word uttered second that occurs as a response, called acceptance; this is the definition of the majority, but in Fath al-Qadir he differed and defined it as the action that occurs second. He said: We only say it is the action, general including acceptance, for among the branches is if one says “Eat” and he eats this food for a dirham, the sale is completed and eating it is permissible, and riding and wearing after the seller says “Ride it for a hundred” and “Dress him for such” is consent to the sale. Similarly, if he says “I sold it to you for a thousand” and he takes possession without saying anything, his taking possession is acceptance, unlike the sale of mu`atah (mutual giving) which has no offer but only taking possession after knowing the price. So considering the case of taking possession after his saying “I sold it to you for a thousand” as a form of mu`atah as some have done is subject to scrutiny. There is no need to change the statement of the scholars, and what he mentioned of branches is only from the angle that an action stands in place of acceptance, hence in al-Khaniyyah: Taking possession stands in place of acceptance. In al-Tatar Khaniyyah: If one says “I bought this food of yours for a thousand” and he gives it in charity and does so in the session without speaking, it is valid; if they separate, no. The restriction of bindingness by offer and acceptance indicates that when the seller sells and the buyer accepts, there is no need thereafter for the seller's permission. In al-Dhakhirah: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan mentioned a case in the Book of Agency that indicates the estimation of an omitted word before the word “sale” which is the word “ruling”, and his intent is to refute Fath. Then his statement “because the conclusion etc.” only appears in the phrasing of al-Hidayah where he used “concludes” instead of the author's “is binding”, and there is a difference between them. Moreover, what he based his statement on that sale is the sum of offer and acceptance with the link does not benefit, because the meaning becomes that sale which is the sum of the three is concluded by offer and acceptance, i.e., it ties together. Yes, the interpretation of “concludes” as “occurs” becomes clear after reflection.
