An offer must specify a price; silence or disposal of the price before acceptance can invalidate the offer.

هل العقد الفاسد الثاني يفسخ الأول؟
عرض الخلاف الداخلي الحنفي حول فسخ الأول بالعقد الفاسد الثاني

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on whether a second fasid contract rescinds the first valid contract and apply the reasoning (ta'lil) that the fasid is annexed to the sahih.

Core Idea
A second invalid contract can rescind the first valid contract because fasid is annexed to sahih in many rulings.

In this passage, al-Ramli reports an internal Hanafi dispute about the effect of a second invalid contract on a prior valid one. The issue touches on the legal nature of fasid contracts: are they completely ineffective or do they carry some weight? The passage presents two views, with the later Hanafi position favoring rescission based on a key analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two conflicting views within the Hanafi school: the early view (e.g., from al-Nahr) that the first contract is not rescinded, and the later, mufta bihi view (e.g., from Jami' al-Fusulayn and al-Bazzaziyya) that it is rescinded.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
The opposing view says the first contract is not rescinded because 'mawjab al-nazar' (the requirement of consideration) prevents a fasid contract from effecting rescission. This is the position of the author of al-Nahr.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both sides are Hanafi.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response supporting rescission
The response cites the example of buying a silver heart for ten then for nine: the second contract is fasid but it necessarily abrogates the first. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that fasid is annexed to sahih in many rulings, so it can effect rescission.
This reasoning is from al-Bazzazi and Jami' al-Fusulayn.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the second fasid contract rescinds the first, ownership returns to the seller immediately. If not, the buyer retains ownership and the second contract is mere agreement without legal effect.
5
Recognize the tarjih (preferred view)
Later authorities (Jami' al-Fusulayn, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Ramli) adopt the rescission view. This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
Al-Ramli reports this as the determined (jazm) position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (واختلفوا فيما إذا كان الثاني فاسد الخ قال في النهر : ومقتضى النظر أن الأول لا ينفسخ اهـ. قال الرملي : جزم في جامع الفصولين والبزازية بأنه ينفسخ. وفي الحاوي الزاهدي نظر في عدم فسخه حيث قال : وفيه نظر ونص شت بخلافه وكذا قال صاحب الذخيرة فإن الثاني وإن كان فاسداً أنه يتضمن نسخ الأول كما لو اشترى قلب فضة وزنها عشرة بعشرة وتقابضا ثم اشتراه منه بتسعة يتضمن فسخ الأول وإن كان الثاني فاسداً وعلل البزازي وصاحب جامع الفصولين بأنه ملحق بالصحيح في كثير من الأحكام والله تعالى أعلم
His statement: 'And they differed regarding when the second [contract] is invalid...' He said in al-Nahr: The requirement of consideration is that the first is not rescinded. Al-Ramli said: In Jami' al-Fusulayn and al-Bazzaziyya it was determined that it is rescinded. In al-Hawi al-Zahidi there is a consideration against its rescission, where he said: There is consideration and the text of Shath is contrary to it. Likewise the author of al-Dhakhira said that the second, even if invalid, necessarily implies abrogation of the first, as if one bought a heart of silver weighing ten for ten and they exchanged, then he bought it from him for nine: that implies rescission of the first even though the second is invalid. Al-Bazzazi and the author of Jami' al-Fusulayn reasoned that it is attached to the valid in many rulings. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
هذا تعليق الشرح على قول المتن 'واختلفوا' في مسألة العقد الفاسد الثاني. ينقل عن النهر أن مقتضى النظر أن الأول لا ينفسخ، لكن الرملي ينقل الجزم في جامع الفصولين والبزازية بأنه ينفسخ. وفي الحاوي الزاهدي نظر في عدم فسخه. ويؤيد صاحب الذخيرة الفسخ مستدلاً بمثال شراء قلب فضة بعشرة ثم شرائه بتسعة: الثاني فاسد لكنه يفسخ الأول. والتعليل أن الفاسد ملحق بالصحيح في كثير من الأحكام، فكذلك في الفسخ. الخلاف في المسألة داخل المذهب الحنفي، والراجح عند كثير من المتأخرين هو الفسخ.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): إبطال العقد الأول بحيث يعود كل إلى ما كان قبل العقد.
فاسد (fasid): الذي يخل بركن أو شرط لا يبطل أصله لكنه لا ينعقد صحيحاً.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
على الرأي الراجح في النص، هل العقد الفاسد الثاني يفسخ الأول؟
A) لا يفسخ مطلقاً
B) يفسخ بالإجماع
C) يفسخ عند الكثيرين، وهو قول صاحب الذخيرة
D) يفسخ فقط إذا كان الصلح

Key Takeaway
The second invalid contract rescinds the first valid contract according to the later Hanafi jurists, based on the principle that the invalid is annexed to the valid in many rulings.

The Validity of a Second Sulh (Compromise)
Clarification of when a second sulh is valid or invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sulh al-isqat and sulh al-iwad and state which type of second sulh is valid.

Core Idea
A second sulh is invalid only if the first was isqat; if the first was for consideration, a second sulh for different consideration is valid.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a common question about the validity of a second sulh (compromise) between the same parties. The key lies in whether the first sulh was an isqat (dropping of a right) or a sulh with consideration. Understanding this distinction prevents the invalidation of a valid contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of the first sulh
Determine if the first sulh was an isqat (dropping of a right without compensation) or an iwad (compromise with consideration like payment).
This is the decisive factor.
2
Apply the ruling for isqat
If the first sulh was isqat, a second sulh is invalid because the right has already ceased to exist.
Like an acquittal (ibra), it cannot be undone.
3
Apply the ruling for iwad
If the first sulh was for consideration, a second sulh for different consideration is valid and does not rescind the first.
Analogous to a sale: a second sale does not void the first.
4
Understand the analogy to sale
The author draws an explicit comparison to sale: just as a second sale is valid and does not cancel the first, a second sulh-iwaḍ is valid.
This teaches that the ruling is not absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والصلح بعد الصلح الثاني باطل) يعني إذا كان الصلح على سبيل الإسقاط لما في الخلاصة قبيل الثالث من البيوع أن المراد الصلح الذي هو إسقاط ، أما إذا كان الصلح على عوض ثم اصطلحا على عوض آخر فالثاني هو الجائز ولا يفسخ الأول كالبيع. حموي على الأشباه قوله: (وأما الإجارة بعد الإجارة (الخ) قال المؤلف في الأشباه : وأما الإجارة بعد الإجارة من المستأجر الأول فالثانية فسخ للأولى كما في البزازية اهـ. وكأنه رآها بعد فإن تأليف الأشباه متأخر عن هذا الشرح قوله : (وهبة الثمن بعد الإيجاب الخ) قال في التتارخانية وفي الفتاوى : الأصيل إذا قال لغيره بعت منك هذا بألف درهم ووهبت منك الألف فقال المشتري اشتريت صح البيع ولا تجوز البراءة لأن الثمن لم يجب بعد. وفي مجموع النوازل: البيع لا يصح في هذه الصورة لأن هذا في معنى البيع بلا ثمن .اهـ. وقال قبل هذا بصفحة وفي الفتاوي الخلاصة : رجل قال لآخر بعت منك عبدي هذا بعشرة دراهم ووهبت منك العشرة وقال الآخر اشتريت لا يصح البيع، أما إذا باع بكذا من الثمن وقبل المشتري ثم أبرأه من الثمن أو وهبه أو تصدق عليه صح، ولو باعه فسكت عن الثمن ثبت الملك إذا اتصل به القبض في قول أبي يوسف ومحمد
His statement: 'And sulh after sulh, the second is invalid' means if the sulh is by way of dropping (isqat), as in al-Khulasa before the third chapter of sales that what is meant is sulh that is isqat. But if the sulh is for a consideration and then they make another sulh for a different consideration, the second is valid and does not rescind the first, like sale. (Hamawi ala al-Ashbah). His statement: 'As for ijarah after ijarah' – the author said in al-Ashbah: ijarah after ijarah from the first lessee, the second is a rescission of the first, as in al-Bazzaziyya. It is as if he saw it later, since the composition of al-Ashbah is later than this commentary. His statement: 'And hiba of the price after offer' – he said in al-Tatarkhaniyya and in al-Fatawa: The principal if he said to another 'I sold this to you for a thousand dirhams and I gifted you the thousand' and the buyer said 'I bought', the sale is valid and discharge is not allowed because the price is not yet due. In Majmu' al-Nawazil: The sale is invalid in this case because it is like a sale without a price. And earlier in the same page, in al-Fatawa al-Khulasa: A man said to another 'I sold you this slave for ten dirhams and I gifted you the ten' and the other said 'I bought', the sale is not valid. But if he sold for a portion of the price and the buyer accepted, then he discharged him from the price or gifted it or gave charity, it is valid. And if he sold and the buyer remained silent about the price, ownership is established if delivery is connected, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
هذا شرح ثلاث مسائل من المتن: الأولى: الصلح بعد الصلح. يبين الشارح أن المراد بالصلح الثاني الباطل هو صلح الإسقاط (كالإبراء)، أما الصلح على عوض فهو جائز ولا يفسخ الأول كالبيع. الثانية: الإجارة بعد الإجارة. ينقل عن الأشباه أن الإجارة الثانية تفسخ الأولى كما في البزازية. ويلاحظ أن تأليف الأشباه متأخر عن هذا الشرح. الثالثة: هبة الثمن بعد الإيجاب وقبل القبول. ينقل الشارح خلافاً: في التتارخانية والفتاوى يصح البيع ولا يجوز البراءة لأن الثمن لم يجب بعد. وفي مجموع النوازل لا يصح لأنه بيع بلا ثمن. وفي الفتاوى الخلاصة لا يصح أيضاً، لكن لو تم البيع أولاً ثم أبرأه صح. وأخيراً: لو سكت المشتري عن الثمن ثم قبض، يثبت الملك عند أبي يوسف ومحمد.

Key Terms
صلح الإسقاط (sulh al-isqat): صلح يرفع النزاع بإسقاط الحق بلا عوض.
صلح العوض (sulh al-iwad): صلح بعوض (مال أو منفعة) مقابل إسقاط الحق.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when is a second sulh valid?
A) When the first sulh was isqat
B) When the first sulh was iwad
C) Always
D) Never

Key Takeaway
A second sulh is invalid only if the first sulh was an isqat; if it was for consideration, a new sulh is valid.

The Effect of a Second Ijarah (Lease) on the First
Ruling that a second ijarah by the same lessee rescinds the first

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a second ijarah by the original lessee constitutes a rescission of the first ijarah.

Core Idea
A second ijarah by the first lessee rescinds the first ijarah — it is a faskh, not a new independent contract.

The source deals with a scenario where the same lessee (musta'jir) enters into a second ijarah after the first, without termination. The commentator clarifies that the second ijarah acts as a rescission of the first, drawing from the text of al-Ashbah. This principle ensures clarity in lease contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
The second ijarah is made by the same lessee (al-musta'jir al-awwal) with the same lessor or a different party? The text specifies 'from the first lessee' implying the same person.
2
Apply the ruling
The second ijarah is considered a faskh (rescission) of the first.
This is the ruling from al-Bazzaziyya as cited.
3
Recognize the implication
The first ijarah is terminated; obligations under it cease.
This prevents double liability.
4
Note the commentary nuance
The commentator observes that the author of al-Ashbah saw this ruling later (since al-Ashbah was written after this sharh).
This is a chronological note, not a substantive change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والصلح بعد الصلح الثاني باطل) يعني إذا كان الصلح على سبيل الإسقاط لما في الخلاصة قبيل الثالث من البيوع أن المراد الصلح الذي هو إسقاط ، أما إذا كان الصلح على عوض ثم اصطلحا على عوض آخر فالثاني هو الجائز ولا يفسخ الأول كالبيع. حموي على الأشباه قوله: (وأما الإجارة بعد الإجارة (الخ) قال المؤلف في الأشباه : وأما الإجارة بعد الإجارة من المستأجر الأول فالثانية فسخ للأولى كما في البزازية اهـ. وكأنه رآها بعد فإن تأليف الأشباه متأخر عن هذا الشرح قوله : (وهبة الثمن بعد الإيجاب الخ) قال في التتارخانية وفي الفتاوى : الأصيل إذا قال لغيره بعت منك هذا بألف درهم ووهبت منك الألف فقال المشتري اشتريت صح البيع ولا تجوز البراءة لأن الثمن لم يجب بعد. وفي مجموع النوازل: البيع لا يصح في هذه الصورة لأن هذا في معنى البيع بلا ثمن .اهـ. وقال قبل هذا بصفحة وفي الفتاوي الخلاصة : رجل قال لآخر بعت منك عبدي هذا بعشرة دراهم ووهبت منك العشرة وقال الآخر اشتريت لا يصح البيع، أما إذا باع بكذا من الثمن وقبل المشتري ثم أبرأه من الثمن أو وهبه أو تصدق عليه صح، ولو باعه فسكت عن الثمن ثبت الملك إذا اتصل به القبض في قول أبي يوسف ومحمد
His statement: 'And sulh after sulh, the second is invalid' means if the sulh is by way of dropping (isqat), as in al-Khulasa before the third chapter of sales that what is meant is sulh that is isqat. But if the sulh is for a consideration and then they make another sulh for a different consideration, the second is valid and does not rescind the first, like sale. (Hamawi ala al-Ashbah). His statement: 'As for ijarah after ijarah' – the author said in al-Ashbah: ijarah after ijarah from the first lessee, the second is a rescission of the first, as in al-Bazzaziyya. It is as if he saw it later, since the composition of al-Ashbah is later than this commentary. His statement: 'And hiba of the price after offer' – he said in al-Tatarkhaniyya and in al-Fatawa: The principal if he said to another 'I sold this to you for a thousand dirhams and I gifted you the thousand' and the buyer said 'I bought', the sale is valid and discharge is not allowed because the price is not yet due. In Majmu' al-Nawazil: The sale is invalid in this case because it is like a sale without a price. Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): إبطال العقد وإنهاؤه قبل نهايته.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what effect does a second ijarah by the original lessee have on the first ijarah?
A) It extends the first ijarah
B) It rescinds the first ijarah
C) It has no effect
D) It invalidates both

Key Takeaway
A second ijarah by the same lessee rescinds the first ijarah; it is a faskh, not a new independent contract.

Hibat al-Thaman (Gift of Price) After Offer: Validity and Conditions
Examination of conflicting rulings on gifting the purchase price before acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate the rulings when a seller gifts the price to the buyer before acceptance vs. after the sale is complete, and apply the correct ruling based on Hanafi texts.

Core Idea
Gifting the price before acceptance makes the sale invalid (like a sale without price); after acceptance, the sale is valid and the gift acts as a discharge.

This passage tackles a subtle issue: what if the seller says 'I sold this to you for X, and I gift you the X' before the buyer accepts? Different Hanafi sources give conflicting answers. The commentator reconciles them by distinguishing timing: before acceptance, the sale is invalid because the price is not yet due; after acceptance and delivery, the gift is valid as a discharge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario with combined offer and gift
The seller says 'I sold you this item for 10 dirhams, and I gift you the 10 dirhams.' The buyer accepts.
This is the core disputed case.
2
Apply the ruling from al-Tatarkhaniyya/Fatawa
Sale is valid but the gift (discharge) is invalid because the price was not yet due.
The price becomes due only after the contract is completed.
3
Apply the ruling from Majmu' al-Nawazil and al-Khulasa
The sale is invalid because it is effectively a sale without a price (gharar).
This is the stricter view.
4
Distinguish the case where sale is complete first
If the sale is finalized and then the seller discharges/gifts the price, the sale is valid and the gift is effective.
This is agreed upon.
5
Consider the case of silence
If the buyer accepts without mentioning the price, and delivery occurs, ownership is established according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
This is a separate ruling about silent acceptance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والصلح بعد الصلح الثاني باطل) يعني إذا كان الصلح على سبيل الإسقاط لما في الخلاصة قبيل الثالث من البيوع أن المراد الصلح الذي هو إسقاط ، أما إذا كان الصلح على عوض ثم اصطلحا على عوض آخر فالثاني هو الجائز ولا يفسخ الأول كالبيع. حموي على الأشباه قوله: (وأما الإجارة بعد الإجارة (الخ) قال المؤلف في الأشباه : وأما الإجارة بعد الإجارة من المستأجر الأول فالثانية فسخ للأولى كما في البزازية اهـ. وكأنه رآها بعد فإن تأليف الأشباه متأخر عن هذا الشرح قوله : (وهبة الثمن بعد الإيجاب الخ) قال في التتارخانية وفي الفتاوى : الأصيل إذا قال لغيره بعت منك هذا بألف درهم ووهبت منك الألف فقال المشتري اشتريت صح البيع ولا تجوز البراءة لأن الثمن لم يجب بعد. وفي مجموع النوازل: البيع لا يصح في هذه الصورة لأن هذا في معنى البيع بلا ثمن .اهـ. وقال قبل هذا بصفحة وفي الفتاوي الخلاصة : رجل قال لآخر بعت منك عبدي هذا بعشرة دراهم ووهبت منك العشرة وقال الآخر اشتريت لا يصح البيع، أما إذا باع بكذا من الثمن وقبل المشتري ثم أبرأه من الثمن أو وهبه أو تصدق عليه صح، ولو باعه فسكت عن الثمن ثبت الملك إذا اتصل به القبض في قول أبي يوسف ومحمد
His statement: 'And sulh after sulh, the second is invalid' means if the sulh is by way of dropping (isqat), as in al-Khulasa before the third chapter of sales that what is meant is sulh that is isqat. But if the sulh is for a consideration and then they make another sulh for a different consideration, the second is valid and does not rescind the first, like sale. (Hamawi ala al-Ashbah). His statement: 'As for ijarah after ijarah' – the author said in al-Ashbah: ijarah after ijarah from the first lessee, the second is a rescission of the first, as in al-Bazzaziyya. It is as if he saw it later, since the composition of al-Ashbah is later than this commentary. His statement: 'And hiba of the price after offer' – he said in al-Tatarkhaniyya and in al-Fatawa: The principal if he said to another 'I sold this to you for a thousand dirhams and I gifted you the thousand' and the buyer said 'I bought', the sale is valid and discharge is not allowed because the price is not yet due. In Majmu' al-Nawazil: The sale is invalid in this case because it is like a sale without a price. And earlier in the same page, in al-Fatawa al-Khulasa: A man said to another 'I sold you this slave for ten dirhams and I gifted you the ten' and the other said 'I bought', the sale is not valid. But if he sold for a portion of the price and the buyer accepted, then he discharged him from the price or gifted it or gave charity, it is valid. And if he sold and the buyer remained silent about the price, ownership is established if delivery is connected, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Commentary
هذا شرح ثلاث مسائل من المتن: الأولى: الصلح بعد الصلح. يبين الشارح أن المراد بالصلح الثاني الباطل هو صلح الإسقاط (كالإبراء)، أما الصلح على عوض فهو جائز ولا يفسخ الأول كالبيع. الثانية: الإجارة بعد الإجارة. ينقل عن الأشباه أن الإجارة الثانية تفسخ الأولى كما في البزازية. ويلاحظ أن تأليف الأشباه متأخر عن هذا الشرح. الثالثة: هبة الثمن بعد الإيجاب وقبل القبول. ينقل الشارح خلافاً: في التتارخانية والفتاوى يصح البيع ولا يجوز البراءة لأن الثمن لم يجب بعد. وفي مجموع النوازل لا يصح لأنه بيع بلا ثمن. وفي الفتاوى الخلاصة لا يصح أيضاً، لكن لو تم البيع أولاً ثم أبرأه صح. وأخيراً: لو سكت المشتري عن الثمن ثم قبض، يثبت الملك عند أبي يوسف ومحمد.

Key Terms
هبة الثمن (hibat al-thaman): هبة الثمن من البائع للمشتري قبل إيجاب الثمن أو بعده.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling when a seller says 'I sold you this for 10 and I gift you the 10' and the buyer accepts?
A) The sale is valid and the buyer owes 10
B) The sale is invalid
C) The sale is valid and the buyer owes nothing
D) The sale is suspended

Key Takeaway
Gifting the price simultaneously with the offer invalidates the sale because it negates genuine consideration; the sale must be completed first for the gift to be effective.

Admission in Sale and the Messenger's Statement
Critical commentary on three sale sub-rulings and source attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state three rulings on admission in sale and explain why the messenger's statement is equated to the sender's, and identify a common error in source attribution.

Core Idea
A buyer's admission after denial is valid, and the messenger's word binds like the sender's – but only if the seller explicitly says 'it reached'.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq delves into three nuanced issues in sales: denial after admission, al-Sighnaqi's restriction to the session, and sale via a messenger. The commentator Ibn Nujaym not only clarifies the rulings but also critiques the author of al-Tatarkhaniyya for omitting source attributions. As we walk through these cases, you will learn how Hanafi jurists handle conflicting reports and the importance of precise citation in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first issue: denial after admission
The seller says 'I sold to you', the buyer denies, then later accepts. The ruling from al-Tatarkhaniyya is that the sale is valid regardless of whether acceptance occurs in the same session or later. Note that this applies to both sale and marriage.
The commentator asks to reflect on why this is valid, implying it may be counterintuitive.
2
Examine al-Sighnaqi's restriction
Al-Sighnaqi restricts the validity to acceptance occurring in the same session. The commentator notes that this restriction is given in al-Tatarkhaniyya without clear reasoning, so further reflection is needed.
This shows an intra-madhhab difference that requires careful consideration of the underlying rationale.
3
Analyze the sale via a messenger
The ruling from al-Khulasa: if the seller says 'I sold it to so-and-so, and it reached (بلغه) and the messenger reached him, and the buyer says I bought', it is valid. If the seller omits 'بلغه', the sale is not valid. The messenger's statement is treated like the sender's.
The key condition is that the seller explicitly mentions the reaching of the offer to the buyer.
4
Understand the source critique
Ibn Nujaym points out that al-Tatarkhaniyya correctly attributed the two differing rulings (valid/invalid) to two separate books, but the author of al-Bahr omitted this attribution. This highlights the importance of tracing rulings to their original sources.
This is a methodological lesson: always check the authority level of a ruling and its attribution.

Source Text

قوله : (وإنكار الإيجاب بعد الإقرار به لا يبطله الخ) الذي رأيته في التتارخانية هكذا : رجل قال لآخر كنت بعت منك هذا العبد بألف درهم وقال الآخر لم أشتره منك فسكت البائع حتى قال المشتري في المجلس أو بعدما افترقا قد اشتريت بألف منك جاز وكذا النكاح اهـ. فليتأمل . قوله : ( وقيده السغناقي في المجلس كذا في التتارخانية ولم يظهر وجهه فتأمل. قوله: (ولو قال بعته من فلان الرسول) كذا في النسخ وفيه سقط. وعبارة التتارخانية: ولو قال بعته من فلان فبلغه فبلغه الرسول فقال المشتري اشتريت لا يصح انتهت. وقوله «لا يصح مخالف لقوله قبله جاز لكن صاحب التتارخانية عز الحكمين إلى كتابين لا كما فعل المؤلف من تركه العزو وعبارة الخلاصة : رجل قال لآخر بعت هذا العبد من فلان فبلغه فبلغه الرسول فقال اشتريت جاز لأن قول الرسول كقول المرسل، ولو لم يقل بلغه فبلغه وقال المشتري اشتريت لا يصح اهـ.
His statement: 'And denial of the offer after admission does not invalidate it etc.' What I saw in al-Tatarkhaniyya is thus: A man said to another 'I had sold this slave to you for a thousand dirhams' and the other said 'I did not buy it from you.' The seller remained silent until the buyer in the session or after they separated said 'I have bought from you for a thousand', it is valid, and likewise marriage. So reflect. His statement: 'And al-Sighnaqi restricted it to the session' – thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya and its reasoning is not apparent, so reflect. His statement: 'If he said, I sold it to so-and-so the messenger' – thus in the copies, and there is an omission. The wording of al-Tatarkhaniyya: If he said 'I sold it to so-and-so' and it reached and the messenger reached him and the buyer said 'I bought', it is not valid. End. And his statement 'it is not valid' contradicts what he said before 'it is valid', but the author of al-Tatarkhaniyya attributed the two rulings to two books, not as the author (of al-Bahr) did in omitting the attribution. The wording of al-Khulasa: A man said to another 'I sold this slave to so-and-so' and it reached him and the messenger reached him and the buyer said 'I bought', it is valid because the messenger's statement is like the statement of the sender. If he did not say 'it reached' but it reached, and the buyer said 'I bought', it is not valid. End.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
هذا تعليق الشارح ابن نجيم على ثلاث مسائل من المتن. الأولى: إنكار الإيجاب بعد الإقرار. ينقل الشارح عبارة التتارخانية التي فيها أن الرجل إذا قال كنت بعتك ثم أنكر المشتري ثم أقر بعد ذلك في المجلس أو بعده جاز البيع. ويطلب التأمل لعلة ذلك. الثانية: تقييد السغناقي لقبول المشتري بالمجلس. يقول الشارح إن هذا التقييد مذكور في التتارخانية لكن وجهه غير واضح، فيطلب التأمل. الثالثة: مسألة 'بعته من فلان الرسول'. يبين أن في النسخ سقطاً، ثم ينقل عبارة التتارخانية التي فيها أن البيع لا يصح إذا بلغ الرسول فقال اشتريت. ثم يلاحظ أن هذه العبارة تخالف ما نقله قبلها من الجواز، ولكن صاحب التتارخانية نسب الحكمين إلى كتابين مختلفين، بخلاف صاحب البحر الذي ترك العزو. ثم ينقل عبارة الخلاصة التي تفرق بين حالة ذكر 'بلغه' فبلغه الرسول (جاز) وحالة عدم ذكر 'بلغه' (لا يصح). هذا التعليق نقدي يحاول تحرير النقل عن المصادر.

Key Terms
رسول (rasul): A person who conveys the offer or acceptance in a sale; his statement is treated as the statement of the sender according to the Hanafis.
الإقرار بالبيع (al-iqrar bil-bay'): Admission of a sale, e.g., a seller saying 'I sold to you' or a buyer saying 'I bought'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Khulasa, when is a sale via a messenger valid?
A) When the messenger is a trustworthy person.
B) When the seller says 'بلغه' and the messenger conveys it to the buyer.
C) When the buyer accepts in the same session as the offer.
D) When the seller personally informs the buyer before the messenger.

Key Takeaway
Admission in sale is binding even after denial, and a messenger's statement is equivalent to the sender's only when the sender explicitly mentions the communication.
